<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In the opinion of management, the unaudited
interim consolidated condensed financial statements of Applied
Materials, Inc. and its subsidiaries (Applied) included herein
have been prepared on a basis consistent with the
October&nbsp;26, 2003 audited consolidated financial statements
and include all material adjustments, consisting of normal
recurring adjustments, necessary to fairly present the
information set forth therein. These unaudited interim
consolidated condensed financial statements should be read in
conjunction with the audited consolidated financial statements
and the accompanying notes thereto included in Applied&#146;s
Form&nbsp;10-K for the fiscal year ended October&nbsp;26, 2003.
Applied&#146;s results of operations for the three and six
months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004 are not necessarily indicative of
future operating results.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The preparation of financial statements in
conformity with generally accepted accounting principles in the
United States of America (United States) requires management to
make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported
in the financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual
results could differ materially from those estimates.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s fiscal year ends on the last
Sunday in October of each year. Fiscal 2004 will contain
53&nbsp;weeks, whereas fiscal 2003 contained 52&nbsp;weeks. The
first fiscal quarter of 2004 contained 14&nbsp;weeks, whereas
the first fiscal quarter of 2003 contained 13&nbsp;weeks.
Accordingly, the first six months of fiscal 2004 contained
27&nbsp;weeks, whereas the first six months of fiscal 2003
contained 26&nbsp;weeks.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Certain prior year amounts have been reclassified
to conform to the fiscal 2004 financial statement presentation.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Stock-Based Compensation</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied measures compensation expense for its
stock-based employee compensation plans using the intrinsic
value method. As the exercise price of all options granted under
these plans was equal to the fair market price of the underlying
common stock on the grant date, no stock-based employee
compensation expense was recognized in the consolidated
condensed statements of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In accordance with Statement of Financial
Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;148, &#147;Accounting for
Stock-based Compensation&nbsp;&#151; Transition and
Disclosure&nbsp;&#151; an Amendment of Financial Accounting
Standards Board (FASB)&nbsp;Statement No.&nbsp;123&#148;
(SFAS&nbsp;148) and Statement of Financial Accounting Standards
No.&nbsp;123, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based
Compensation&#148; (SFAS&nbsp;123), Applied&#146;s pro forma
option expense is computed using the Black-Scholes option
pricing model. This model was developed for use in estimating
the value of publicly traded options that have no vesting
restrictions and are fully transferable. Applied&#146;s employee
stock options have characteristics significantly different from
those of traded options; therefore, in the opinion of
management, the Black-Scholes option pricing model generally
used to comply with SFAS&nbsp;148 and SFAS&nbsp;123 does not
necessarily provide a reliable measure of the fair value of
Applied&#146;s options.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">To comply with SFAS&nbsp;148, Applied is
presenting the following table to illustrate the effect on the
net income/(loss) and earnings/(loss) per share if it had
applied the fair value recognition provisions of
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">5
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Based on the Black-Scholes option pricing model,
the weighted average estimated fair value of employee stock
option grants was $5.97 and $9.82 for the three months ended
April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004, respectively, and was
$6.27 and $10.41 for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
and May&nbsp;2, 2004, respectively. The weighted average
estimated fair value of purchase rights under employee stock
purchase plans (ESPP)&nbsp;was $4.11 and $5.94 for the three
months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004,
respectively. For the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 and
May&nbsp;2, 2004, the weighted average estimated fair value of
purchase rights under ESPP was $4.90 and $5.90, respectively.
For purposes of this calculation, the fair value of each stock
option grant and stock purchase right is estimated on the date
of grant using the Black-Scholes option pricing model and the
following assumptions:
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">2)&nbsp;Earnings/(Loss) Per Share</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Basic earnings/(loss) per share has been
determined using the weighted average number of common shares
outstanding during the period. In the event of a net loss, basic
loss per share is the same as diluted loss per share. Diluted
earnings per share has been determined using the weighted
average number of common
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">6
</FONT>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">APPLIED MATERIALS, INC.</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED CONDENSED FINANCIAL
STATEMENTS&nbsp;&#151;&nbsp;(Continued)</FONT></B>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">(Unaudited)</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">shares and equivalents (representing the dilutive
effect of stock options) outstanding during the period.
Applied&#146;s net income/(loss) has not been adjusted for any
period presented for purposes of computing basic or diluted
earnings/(loss) per share.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For purposes of computing diluted earnings per
share, weighted average common share equivalents do not include
stock options with an exercise price that exceeded the average
fair market value of Applied&#146;s common stock for the period,
as the effect would be anti-dilutive. Anti-dilutive options that
were excluded from the computation were as follows:

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">3)&nbsp;Accounts Receivable, Net</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied has agreements with various financial
institutions to sell accounts receivable from selected
customers. Applied sold accounts receivable under these
agreements of $172&nbsp;million and $184&nbsp;million for the
three months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004,
respectively, and sold $294&nbsp;million and $352&nbsp;million
for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2,
2004, respectively. Discounting fees were not material for all
periods presented, and were recorded as interest expense. As of
May&nbsp;2, 2004, $58&nbsp;million of sold receivables remained
outstanding under these agreements. A portion of these sold
receivables is subject to certain recourse provisions. Applied
has not experienced any losses under these recourse provisions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In connection with the adoption of Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and
Other Intangible Assets&#148; (SFAS&nbsp;142), as of the
beginning of fiscal 2002, goodwill is no longer amortized and is
reviewed annually during the fourth fiscal quarter for
impairment. From October&nbsp;27, 2003 to May&nbsp;2, 2004, the
change in goodwill was approximately $7&nbsp;million, which
primarily consisted of adjustments to the purchase price for
prior acquisitions containing contingent purchase price
provisions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Gross purchased technology increased by
$8&nbsp;million due to purchased technology acquired during the
second fiscal quarter of 2004. Purchased technology and other
intangible assets are amortized over their estimated useful
lives of five to 10&nbsp;years using the straight-line method.
Aggregate amortization expense was $12&nbsp;million and
$13&nbsp;million for the three months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
and May&nbsp;2, 2004, respectively and $24&nbsp;million and
$25&nbsp;million for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
and May&nbsp;2, 2004, respectively. As of May&nbsp;2, 2004,
future estimated amortization expense is expected to be
$25&nbsp;million for the remainder of fiscal 2004,
$21&nbsp;million for fiscal 2005, $15&nbsp;million for fiscal
2006, $7&nbsp;million for fiscal 2007, $4&nbsp;million for
fiscal 2008 and $3&nbsp;million thereafter.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied has a venture capital fund, Applied
Materials Ventures&nbsp;I, L.P. (the Fund), that invests in
privately-held, early-stage companies engaged in developing
systems, components and devices relating to nanotechnology
and/or communications technology for specific applications and
products. The Fund is a limited partnership with Applied as the
sole limited partner and an independent party as the general
partner. Applied has committed to fund $50&nbsp;million in
capital contributions, but has reserved the option to
discontinue capital contributions at $25&nbsp;million.
Applied&#146;s capital contributions to the Fund totaled
approximately $16&nbsp;million through October&nbsp;26, 2003 and
$19&nbsp;million through May&nbsp;2, 2004.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied products are generally sold with a
12-month warranty period following installation. Parts and labor
are covered under the terms of the warranty agreement. The
warranty provision is based on historical experience by product,
configuration and geographic region. Quarterly warranty
consumption is associated with sales that occurred during the
preceding four quarters, and quarterly warranty provisions are
generally related to the current quarter&#146;s sales.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the ordinary course of business, Applied
also provides standby letters of credit or other guarantee
agreements to certain parties as required for certain
transactions initiated by either Applied or its subsidiaries. As
of May&nbsp;2, 2004, the maximum potential amount of future
payments that Applied could be required to make under these
guarantee agreements was approximately $56&nbsp;million. Applied
has not recorded any liability in connection with these
guarantee agreements beyond that required to appropriately
account for the underlying transaction being guaranteed. Applied
does not believe, based on historical experience and information
currently available, that it is probable that any amounts will
be required to be paid under these guarantee agreements.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied also has additional guarantee agreements
on behalf of certain subsidiaries. As of May&nbsp;2, 2004,
Applied has not recorded any liability related to guarantees of
subsidiary obligations. Applied does not expect, based on
historical experience and information currently available, that
it is probable any amounts will be required to be paid under
these agreements. Subsidiary guarantees as of May&nbsp;2, 2004
were associated with the following types of agreements:
short-term borrowings, overdrafts and leases. While certain
subsidiaries had
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">short-term borrowings and overdraft facilities
available totaling approximately $172&nbsp;million as of
May&nbsp;2, 2004, no amounts were outstanding as of the end of
the second fiscal quarter of 2004. In the event of use and
subsequent default of these facilities by Applied&#146;s
subsidiaries, such agreements would be guaranteed by Applied. In
addition, certain subsidiaries have lease agreements guaranteed
by Applied. These leases will expire between 2009 and 2014. In
the event that the subsidiaries do not make the required
payments, Applied could be required to pay the leases on behalf
of the subsidiaries. As of May&nbsp;2, 2004, quarterly lease
obligations under these agreements approximated $3&nbsp;million.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In connection with certain business combinations
and purchased technology acquisitions, Applied was subject to
contingent consideration agreements at May&nbsp;2, 2004. These
agreements are based upon sales volume or other events taking
place subsequent to the acquisition. Depending upon the
circumstances of each agreement, the payment of the contingency
will result in an increase to goodwill or a charge to operating
expenses. Amounts paid under these agreements have not had, and
are not expected to have, a material effect on Applied&#146;s
financial condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied is subject to various legal proceedings
and claims, either asserted or unasserted, that arise in the
ordinary course of business. Applied from time to time is, and
in the future may be, involved in legal proceedings or claims
regarding patent infringement, intellectual property rights,
antitrust, environmental regulations, securities, contracts,
product performance, product liability, employment and other
matters. In addition, Applied on occasion receives notification
from customers who believe that Applied owes them
indemnification or other obligations related to infringement
claims made against the customers by third parties. Applied
evaluates, among other factors, the degree of probability of an
unfavorable outcome and reasonably estimates the amount of the
loss. Significant judgment is required in evaluating these
factors. When Applied determines that it is probable that a loss
has been incurred, the effect is recorded in the consolidated
financial statements. Significant changes in legal proceedings
and claims or in the factors considered in the evaluation of
those matters could have a material adverse effect on
Applied&#146;s business, financial condition and results of
operations. Discussion of legal matters is incorporated by
reference from Part&nbsp;II, Item&nbsp;1, Legal Proceedings, of
this report, and should be considered as an integral part of the
Consolidated Condensed Financial Statements and the accompanying
Notes.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">7)&nbsp;Restructuring, Asset Impairments and
Other Charges</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In response to difficult business conditions
during fiscal year 2003, Applied implemented a series of
realignment activities. These actions were intended to better
align Applied&#146;s cost structure with prevailing economic
conditions. As of February&nbsp;1, 2004, Applied had completed
its realignment activities.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring, asset impairments and other
charges for the first fiscal quarter of 2004 totaled
$167&nbsp;million, consisting of $65&nbsp;million for facility
consolidations, $96&nbsp;million for other costs and
$6&nbsp;million for severance and benefits. The $96&nbsp;million
of other costs primarily consisted of $102&nbsp;million in fixed
asset write-offs associated with facility consolidations during
the first fiscal quarter of 2004, which was partially offset by
a $6&nbsp;million reversal of fixed asset reserves associated
with prior periods&#146; restructuring plans. In connection with
the restructuring action in the first fiscal quarter of 2004,
Applied consolidated certain facilities located primarily in
Santa&nbsp;Clara, California. Additionally, Applied reduced its
global workforce by approximately 130 positions or one percent.
The majority of the affected employees were based in
Santa&nbsp;Clara, California and Europe and represented multiple
company functions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring, asset impairments, and other
charges were $93&nbsp;million for the second fiscal quarter of
2003. As part of this restructuring, Applied reduced its
infrastructure and global workforce by approximately 1,400
positions or 10&nbsp;percent. The majority of the affected
employees were based in Santa&nbsp;Clara, California and Austin,
Texas and represented multiple company functions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">8)&nbsp;Derivative Financial
Instruments</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s derivative financial instruments,
consisting of forward exchange and option contracts, are
recorded at fair value on the balance sheet, either in other
current assets or accounts payable and accrued expenses. Changes
in the fair value of derivatives that do not qualify for hedge
treatment, as well as the ineffective portion of any hedges, are
recognized currently in results of operations. The effective
portion of the gain or loss is reported as a component of
accumulated other comprehensive income in stockholders&#146;
equity, and is reclassified into results of operations when the
hedged transaction affects income/(loss). All amounts included
in accumulated other comprehensive income as of May&nbsp;2, 2004
will be reclassified to results of operations within
12&nbsp;months. Changes in the fair value of currency option
contracts due to changes in time value are excluded from the
assessment of effectiveness, and are recognized in cost of
products sold. The change in option time value was not material
for all periods presented. If the transaction being hedged fails
to occur, or if a portion of any derivative is deemed to be
ineffective, Applied recognizes the gain or loss on the
associated financial instrument in general and administrative
expenses. The amounts recognized due to the anticipated
transactions failing to occur were not material for all periods
presented.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Accumulated other comprehensive income related to
derivative activities for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004
increased by $4&nbsp;million, which was comprised of a
$7&nbsp;million net increase in fair value of derivatives,
partially offset by $3&nbsp;million of net realized gains which
were reclassified from accumulated other comprehensive income to
results of operations.
</FONT>

<TR valign="top">

    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Stock Repurchase Program</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Since March 1996, Applied has systematically
repurchased shares of its common stock to partially fund its
stock-based employee benefit plans. Upon the expiration of the
prior share repurchase authorization on March&nbsp;24, 2004, the
Board of Directors extended the stock repurchase program and
authorized the repurchase of up to $3&nbsp;billion of
Applied&#146;s common stock in the open market over the
succeeding three years. Under this authorization, Applied is
continuing a systematic stock repurchase program and may also
make additional stock repurchases from time to time, depending
on market conditions, stock price and other factors.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the three months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
and May&nbsp;2, 2004, Applied repurchased 3,995,000&nbsp;shares
of its common stock at an average price of $12.52 for a total
cash outlay of $50&nbsp;million and 3,538,000&nbsp;shares of its
common stock at an average price of $21.20 for a total cash
outlay of $75&nbsp;million, respectively. During the six months
ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004, Applied
repurchased 7,068,000&nbsp;shares of its common stock at an
average price of $14.14, for a total cash outlay of
$100&nbsp;million and 6,791,000&nbsp;shares of its common stock
at an average price of $22.09 for a total cash outlay of
$150&nbsp;million, respectively.
</FONT>

$673&nbsp;million, of which $500&nbsp;million is comprised of
two revolving credit agreements in the United States with
</FONT>

The agreements provide for borrowings at various rates,
including the lead bank&#146;s prime reference rate, and include
financial and other covenants with which Applied was in
compliance as of October&nbsp;26, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004. No
amounts were outstanding under these agreements as of
October&nbsp;26, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004. The remaining credit
facilities of approximately $173&nbsp;million are with Japanese
banks at rates indexed to their prime reference rate and are
denominated in Japanese yen. No amounts were outstanding under
Japanese credit facilities as of October&nbsp;26, 2003 and
May&nbsp;2, 2004.

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">11)&nbsp;Business Combination</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;18, 2003, Applied acquired Boxer
Cross, Inc., a producer of in-line monitoring systems that
provide customers with critical electrical measurement data for
controlling semiconductor processes, for $14&nbsp;million in
cash. In connection with this acquisition, Applied recorded
goodwill of $18&nbsp;million, net of adjustments to the initial
purchase price allocation, and purchased technology of
$3&nbsp;million, partially offset by other items of
$7&nbsp;million, primarily for net liabilities assumed upon
acquisition. The in-process research and development expense was
insignificant. The results of operations for Boxer Cross, Inc.
prior to the acquisition date were not material in relation to
those of Applied for any of the periods presented herein.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">12)&nbsp;Recent Accounting
Pronouncement</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On December&nbsp;17, 2003, the Securities and
Exchange Commission issued Staff Accounting Bulletin
No.&nbsp;104, &#147;Revenue Recognition&#148; (SAB&nbsp;104),
which superceded Staff Accounting Bulletin No.&nbsp;101,
&#147;Revenue Recognition in Financial Statements&#148;
(SAB&nbsp;101). The revenue recognition principles of
SAB&nbsp;101 remain largely unchanged by the issuance of
SAB&nbsp;104. SAB&nbsp;104 also recognized the existing guidance
on revenue arrangements with multiple deliverables. The adoption
of SAB&nbsp;104 has not had, and is not expected to have, a
material effect on Applied&#146;s financial condition or results
of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Overview</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied develops, manufactures, markets and
services integrated circuit fabrication equipment for the
worldwide semiconductor industry. Applied&#146;s product
offerings consist of systems, components, spare parts, and
services. Demand for Applied&#146;s products can change
significantly from period to period as a result of numerous
factors, including, but not limited to, changes in:
(1)&nbsp;global economic conditions; (2)&nbsp;advanced
technology and/or capacity requirements of semiconductor
manufacturers; (3)&nbsp;the profitability of semiconductor
manufacturers; (4)&nbsp;supply and demand for semiconductors;
and (5)&nbsp;relative competitiveness of Applied&#146;s
products. For this and other reasons, Applied&#146;s results of
operations for the three and six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004
may not necessarily be indicative of future operating results.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Beginning with the fourth fiscal quarter of 2003
and continuing into fiscal 2004, customers began making
increased investments in capacity and technology, responding to
higher spending for consumer electronics and business
information technology and increases in semiconductor unit
demand. The past industry downturn, extending from the first
fiscal quarter of 2001 through the third fiscal quarter of 2003,
which Applied believes was the most severe decline in the
history of the semiconductor industry, resulted in a significant
decrease in demand for semiconductor manufacturing equipment,
lower investment in fab capacity, and customers&#146; delays in
placing new orders.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Fiscal 2004 will contain 53&nbsp;weeks, whereas
fiscal 2003 contained 52&nbsp;weeks. The first fiscal quarter of
2004 contained 14&nbsp;weeks, whereas the first fiscal quarter
of 2003 contained 13&nbsp;weeks. Accordingly, the first six
months of fiscal 2004 contained 27&nbsp;weeks, whereas the first
six months of fiscal 2003 contained 26&nbsp;weeks.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Results of Operations</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied received new orders of $2.2&nbsp;billion
for the second fiscal quarter of 2004, compared to
$1.7&nbsp;billion for the first fiscal quarter of 2004 and
$971&nbsp;million for the second fiscal quarter of 2003. New
orders for the second fiscal quarter of 2004 increased by
32&nbsp;percent from the preceding quarter and by
128&nbsp;percent from the second fiscal quarter of 2003. The
increase in orders reflected broad-based capital investment by
customers for 300mm technology, from both DRAM and logic
manufacturers, as well as capacity expansion by customers for
200mm technology to meet rising demand for semiconductors.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">14

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As indicated in the table above, orders increased
during the second fiscal quarter of 2004 throughout all regions,
except for Europe. The order growth in the second fiscal quarter
of 2004 was centered in Asia. Taiwan, Korea and Asia-Pacific
continued the trend of sequential quarterly order growth. Orders
in Japan increased over the preceding fiscal quarter, reflecting
increased capital investment. European orders for the second
fiscal quarter were lower than the prior quarter due to higher
service orders that occurred in the first fiscal quarter of 2004.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s backlog for the most recent three
fiscal quarters was as follows: $2.8&nbsp;billion as of
May&nbsp;2, 2004, $2.6&nbsp;billion as of February&nbsp;1, 2004
and $2.5&nbsp;billion as of October&nbsp;26, 2003. Backlog
consists only of orders for which written authorizations have
been accepted, shipment dates within 12&nbsp;months have been
assigned and revenue has not been recognized. Due to the
potential for customer changes in delivery schedules or
cancellation of orders, Applied&#146;s backlog at any particular
time is not necessarily indicative of actual sales for any
future periods.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Net sales increased to $1.2&nbsp;billion in the
fourth fiscal quarter of 2003 and $1.6&nbsp;billion for the
first fiscal quarter of 2004, after having been relatively flat
at $1.1&nbsp;billion for each of the first three fiscal quarters
of 2003. Net sales for the second fiscal quarter of 2004
increased to $2.0&nbsp;billion, a 30&nbsp;percent increase from
the first fiscal quarter of 2004 and an 82&nbsp;percent increase
from net sales of $1.1&nbsp;billion in the second fiscal quarter
of 2003. The overall increase in net sales was primarily due to
the fulfillment of higher levels of orders for capital equipment
received in prior quarters.
</FONT>

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">**&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">Primarily the United States.
    </FONT></TD>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As indicated in the table above, net sales for
the second fiscal quarter of 2004 increased year over year for
all regions, except for Korea, reflecting a continued
improvement in the worldwide demand for wafer fabrication
equipment. Net sales for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004
increased in all regions with the exception of Korea and North
America over the comparable period in fiscal 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Gross margin was 46.5&nbsp;percent for the second
fiscal quarter of 2004, compared to 43.5&nbsp;percent for the
first fiscal quarter of 2004 and 33.7&nbsp;percent for the
second fiscal quarter of 2003. Gross margin was
45.2&nbsp;percent for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004,
compared to 35.3&nbsp;percent for the six months ended
April&nbsp;27, 2003. A $49&nbsp;million inventory write-down
associated with refocused product efforts was incurred in the
second fiscal quarter of 2003. The increase in the gross margin
percentage from the first fiscal quarter to the second fiscal
quarter of 2004 was principally attributable to improved revenue
levels, declining 300mm product costs and increased
manufacturing volume. The increase in gross margin from the
three and six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 compared to the
same periods ended May&nbsp;2, 2004 was due to the same reasons
discussed above.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Operating expenses included expenses related to
research, development and engineering (RD&#38;E), marketing and
selling (M&#38;S), and general and administrative (G&#38;A).
Expenses related to RD&#38;E, M&#38;S and G&#38;A were
$424&nbsp;million for the second fiscal quarter of 2004,
compared to $411&nbsp;million for the first fiscal quarter of
2004 and $394&nbsp;million for the second fiscal quarter of
2003. The increase in these expenses during the second fiscal
quarter of 2004 was principally attributable to an increase in
variable compensation costs resulting from the current
quarter&#146;s performance, offset by a lower cost structure as
a result of the implementation of realignment activities.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In response to difficult business conditions
during fiscal year 2003, Applied implemented a series of
realignment activities. These actions were intended to better
align Applied&#146;s cost structure with prevailing economic
conditions. As of February&nbsp;1, 2004, Applied had completed
its realignment activities.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring, asset impairments and other
charges for the first fiscal quarter of 2004 totaled
$167&nbsp;million, consisting of $65&nbsp;million for facilities
consolidations, $96&nbsp;million for other costs and
$6&nbsp;million for severance and benefits. The $96&nbsp;million
of other costs primarily consisted of $102&nbsp;million in fixed
asset write-offs associated with facility consolidations during
the first fiscal quarter of 2004, which was partially offset by
a $6&nbsp;million reversal of fixed asset reserves associated
with prior periods&#146; restructuring plans. In connection with
the restructuring action in the first fiscal quarter of 2004,
Applied consolidated certain facilities located primarily in
Santa&nbsp;Clara, California. Additionally, Applied reduced its
global workforce by approximately 130 positions or one percent.
The majority of the affected employees were based in
Santa&nbsp;Clara, California and Europe and represented multiple
company functions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring, asset impairments, and other
charges were $93&nbsp;million for the second fiscal quarter of
2003. As part of this restructuring, Applied reduced its
infrastructure and global workforce by approximately
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">16
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">1,400 positions or 10&nbsp;percent. The majority
of the affected employees were based in Santa&nbsp;Clara,
California and Austin, Texas and represented multiple company
functions.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring, asset impairments and other
charges for the first fiscal quarter of 2003 totaled
$99&nbsp;million, consisting of $80&nbsp;million for severance
and benefits and $19&nbsp;million for facilities consolidations.
In connection with the restructuring action in the first fiscal
quarter of 2003, Applied reduced its global workforce by
approximately 1,750 positions or 11&nbsp;percent. The majority
of the affected employees and facilities were in
Santa&nbsp;Clara, California and Austin, Texas and represented
multiple company functions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Net interest income was $15&nbsp;million and
$26&nbsp;million for the three months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004 and
April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively, and was $34&nbsp;million and
$50&nbsp;million for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004 and
April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively. Lower net interest income in
2004 was primarily due to lower average yields and lower
realized gains.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s effective income tax provision/
(benefit) rate was 29.5&nbsp;percent for all periods presented.
Applied&#146;s future income tax rate depends on various
factors, such as tax legislation and interpretation, the
geographic composition of Applied&#146;s pre-tax income, the
valuation of Applied&#146;s deferred tax assets or liabilities,
and non-tax deductible expenses incurred with acquisitions. In
addition, Applied is subject to routine examination of its tax
returns by the Internal Revenue Service and other tax
authorities. Applied regularly assesses the likelihood of
adverse outcomes from these examinations to determine the
adequacy of its provision for income taxes.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Financial Condition, Liquidity and Capital
Resources</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004,
Applied increased its cash, cash equivalents and short-term
investments by $413&nbsp;million, from $5.5&nbsp;billion as of
October&nbsp;26, 2003 to $5.9&nbsp;billion as of May&nbsp;2,
2004, reflecting improved profitability and asset management.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied generated $438&nbsp;million of cash from
operating activities for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004.
The primary sources of cash were from net income and an increase
in payables, which were partially offset by an increase in
accounts receivable and inventories for the six months ended
May&nbsp;2, 2004. Applied utilized programs to sell accounts
receivable of $352&nbsp;million for the six months ended
May&nbsp;2, 2004. These accounts receivable sales had the effect
of increasing cash and reducing accounts receivable. Applied has
not experienced any losses under these programs. Days sales
outstanding was 63&nbsp;days at the end of the second fiscal
quarter of 2004, compared to 68&nbsp;days at the end of the
first fiscal quarter of 2004. For further details regarding
accounts receivable sales, see Note&nbsp;3 of Notes to
Consolidated Condensed Financial Statements. Inventories
increased by $160&nbsp;million during the six months ended
May&nbsp;2, 2004, due to a $222&nbsp;million increase in raw
materials, work-in-process and finished goods inventories to
support increased business volume, which was partially offset by
a $62&nbsp;million decrease in customer service spares inventory.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied used $449&nbsp;million of cash for
investing activities during the six months ended May&nbsp;2,
2004. Capital expenditures totaled $113&nbsp;million. Applied
utilized $337&nbsp;million in cash for purchases of short-term
investments, net of proceeds from sales and maturities of
short-term investments.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied generated $104&nbsp;million of cash from
financing activities for the six months ended May&nbsp;2, 2004,
primarily consisting of $257&nbsp;million of proceeds from the
issuance of common stock under stock option and employee stock
purchase plans, partially offset by $150&nbsp;million of stock
repurchases.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Although cash requirements will fluctuate based
on the timing and extent of many factors, Applied&#146;s
management believes that cash generated from operations,
together with the liquidity provided by existing cash balances
and borrowing capability, will be sufficient to satisfy
Applied&#146;s liquidity requirements for the next
12&nbsp;months. For further details regarding Applied&#146;s
operating, investing and financing activities, see the
Consolidated Condensed Statements of Cash Flows.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Trends, Risks and Uncertainties</FONT></B>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">The industry that Applied serves is highly
    volatile and unpredictable.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As a supplier to the global semiconductor
industry, Applied is subject to the industry&#146;s business
cycles, the timing, length and volatility of which are difficult
to predict. The semiconductor industry has historically been
cyclical due to sudden changes in demand for semiconductors and
manufacturing capacity, including capacity using the latest
technology. The rate of changes in demand, including
end-customer demand, is accelerating, and the effect of these
changes on Applied is occurring sooner, exacerbating the
volatility of these cycles. These changes have affected the
timing and amounts of customers&#146; capital equipment
purchases and investments in technology, and continue to affect
Applied&#146;s orders, net sales, gross margin and results of
operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The semiconductor industry is in an upturn.
However, management cannot predict the sustainability of such a
recovery, nor the industry&#146;s rate of growth going forward,
both of which will be affected by many factors, including the
uncertainties discussed below. During periods of increasing
demand for integrated circuit manufacturing equipment, Applied
must have sufficient manufacturing capacity and inventory to
meet customer demand, and must be able to attract, retain and
motivate a sufficient number of qualified individuals. If
Applied is unable to effectively manage its resources and
production capacity during an industry upturn, there could be a
material adverse effect on its business, financial condition and
results of operations. Conversely, in downturns, Applied must be
able to appropriately align its cost structure with prevailing
market conditions and effectively motivate and retain key
employees. In the first quarter of 2004, Applied completed
implementation of realignment activities undertaken in response
to an industry downturn to align its cost structure with
business conditions and to enable Applied to focus resources on
core research and development programs. If the intended results
of these realignment activities do not materialize, and/or if
Applied does not maintain effective cost controls,
Applied&#146;s business, financial condition or results of
operations may be materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied is exposed to the risks of
    operating a global business.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the second fiscal quarter of 2004, more
than 85&nbsp;percent of Applied&#146;s net sales were to regions
outside the United States. Certain manufacturing facilities and
suppliers of Applied are also located outside the United States.
Managing Applied&#146;s global operations presents challenges
including, but not limited to, those arising from periodic
regional economic downturns, global trade issues, varying
business conditions and demands, variations in enforcement of
intellectual property and other legal rights in different
jurisdictions, differences in the ability to develop
relationships with suppliers and other local businesses, changes
in United States and international laws and regulations
including United States export restrictions, fluctuations in
interest and currency exchange rates, the need to provide
sufficient levels of technical support in different locations,
cultural differences and shipping delays. Many of these
challenges are present in China, a large potential market for
integrated circuit equipment and an area that Applied
anticipates will present a significant opportunity for growth.
These challenges, as well as global uncertainties with respect
to: (1)&nbsp;economic growth rates in various countries;
(2)&nbsp;sustainability of demand for electronics products;
(3)&nbsp;capital spending by semiconductor manufacturers;
(4)&nbsp;price weakness for certain semiconductor devices; and
(5)&nbsp;political instability, terrorism, acts of war, or
epidemics where Applied has operations or sales, including Asia,
Israel and the United States, may materially and adversely
affect Applied&#146;s business, financial condition and results
of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">18
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied is exposed to risks as a result of
    ongoing changes in the semiconductor industry.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The semiconductor industry is characterized by
rapid ongoing changes, including: (1)&nbsp;more complex
technology requirements; (2)&nbsp;the changing information
technology cost structure and the importance of driving down
cost of ownership; (3)&nbsp;the increasing significance of
consumer electronics as a driver for chip demand and the related
focus on lower prices; (4)&nbsp;the growing types and varieties
of integrated circuits and applications; (5)&nbsp;an increasing
number of applications across multiple substrate sizes in the
semiconductor industry, resulting in divergent interests among
semiconductor manufacturers; (6)&nbsp;a rising percentage of
business from customers in Asia and emergence of customers and
competitors in new geographical regions; (7)&nbsp;customer
demands for shorter lead times for the manufacture and
installation of semiconductor manufacturing equipment; and
(8)&nbsp;higher capital requirements for new semiconductor
fabrication plants. These changes, individually or in
combination, are increasing the need for customer partnering,
use of foundries, collaborative research and development efforts
and process integration support. These changes also heighten the
importance of spare parts and service product offerings as a
competitive advantage for semiconductor equipment manufacturers,
even though service products historically have resulted, and may
in the future result, in lower gross margins than system
products. In addition, key integrated circuit manufacturers have
become influential in technology decisions made by their global
partners. If Applied does not successfully manage the risks
resulting from the ongoing changes occurring in the
semiconductor industry, its business, financial condition and
results of operation could be materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied operates in a highly competitive
    industry characterized by increasingly rapid technological
    changes.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As Applied operates in a highly competitive
environment, Applied&#146;s future success is heavily dependent
on effective development, commercialization and customer
acceptance of its new products and services over those of its
competitors. Applied&#146;s success is subject to many risks,
including but not limited to its ability to timely and
cost-effectively: (1)&nbsp;develop new products, services and
technologies, including those utilizing new materials, such as
copper and low-k films; (2)&nbsp;improve existing products,
services and technologies; (3)&nbsp;expand into or develop new
markets in the semiconductor industry for Applied&#146;s
products and services; (4)&nbsp;introduce new products and
services to the marketplace; (5)&nbsp;achieve market acceptance
and accurately forecast demand for its products and services;
(6)&nbsp;transition from 200mm systems to 300mm systems while
still maintaining sufficient 200mm technological capabilities;
(7)&nbsp;qualify new or improved products for volume
manufacturing with its customers; (8)&nbsp;commence and adjust
production to meet customer demands; (9)&nbsp;price products and
services appropriately; and (10)&nbsp;lower customers&#146; cost
of ownership. The development, introduction and support of an
increasingly broad set of new or improved products, services and
technologies, including those enabling the transition to smaller
device feature sizes, new materials and 300mm wafers, have grown
increasingly complex and expensive over time. Such new or
improved products and services may involve higher costs and
reduced efficiencies compared to Applied&#146;s more established
products and services and could adversely affect Applied&#146;s
gross margins. If Applied does not develop and introduce new or
improved products, services and technologies in a timely and
cost-effective manner in response to changing market conditions
or customer requirements, and/or if Applied is not able to price
such products and services appropriately to reflect increased
costs, its business, financial condition and results of
operations could be materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

    failure to estimate customer demand accurately could result in
    excess or obsolete inventory.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s business depends on its ability to
supply products and services that meet the rapidly changing
demands of its customers, which depends in part on the timely
delivery of parts, components and subassemblies (collectively,
parts) from suppliers. Some key parts may be obtained only from
a single supplier or a limited group of suppliers. In addition,
Applied outsources certain manufacturing activities. Significant
interruptions of manufacturing operations as a result of the
failure or inability of suppliers to timely deliver quality
parts, outsourcing difficulties, natural disasters (such as
earthquakes or tornadoes), or other causes (such as information
technology or infrastructure failures, regional economic
downturns, political instability,
</FONT>

in delayed product or service deliveries or manufacturing
inefficiencies. Conversely, if actual demand for Applied&#146;s
products and services is less than expected, Applied may
purchase more parts than necessary or incur costs for canceling
or postponing delivery of parts. Any or all of these factors
could materially and adversely affect Applied&#146;s business,

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s customer base is and has been
highly concentrated. Orders from a relatively limited number of
manufacturers of integrated circuits have accounted for, and
likely will continue to account for, a substantial portion of
Applied&#146;s net sales, which may lead customers to demand
pricing and other terms less favorable to Applied. In addition,
sales to any single customer may vary significantly from quarter
to quarter. If current customers delay, cancel or do not place
orders, Applied may not be able to replace these orders with new
orders. As Applied&#146;s products are configured to customer
specifications, changing, rescheduling or canceling orders may
result in significant non-recoverable costs. The resulting
fluctuations in the amount of and terms of orders could have a
material adverse effect on Applied&#146;s business, financial
condition and results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied has made, and may in the future make,
acquisitions of, or significant investments in, businesses with
complementary products, services and/or technologies.
Acquisitions involve numerous risks, including but not limited
to: (1)&nbsp;diversion of management&#146;s attention from other
operational matters; (2)&nbsp;the inability to realize expected
synergies resulting from the acquisition; (3)&nbsp;failure to
commercialize purchased technologies; (4) impairment of acquired
intangible assets as a result of technological advancements or
worse-than-expected performance of the acquired company or its
products; (5)&nbsp;integration and retention of key employees;
and (6)&nbsp;integration of operations. Mergers and acquisitions
are inherently subject to significant risks, and the inability
to effectively manage these risks could materially and adversely
affect Applied&#146;s business, financial condition and results
of operations.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;

These service products include on-site support as well as supply
chain and spare parts management and planning. These new service
products may be offered through strategic alliances formed with

strategic relationships with appropriate companies and
successfully and cost-effectively provide these services.
Applied&#146;s inability to achieve any of the foregoing could

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied from time to time is, and in the future
may be, involved in legal proceedings or claims regarding patent
infringement, intellectual property rights, antitrust,
environmental regulations, securities, contracts, product
performance, product liability, employment and other matters. In
addition, Applied on occasion receives notification from
customers who believe that Applied owes them indemnification or
other obligations related to infringement claims made against
the customers by third parties. These legal proceedings and
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">claims, whether with or without merit, are
time-consuming and expensive to prosecute or defend and divert
management&#146;s attention and resources. There can be no
assurance regarding the outcome of current or future legal
proceedings or claims. In addition, Applied&#146;s intellectual

the laws of other countries permit the protection of
Applied&#146;s rights to varying extents, compared to United

result in uncompensated lost market and revenue opportunities
for Applied. If Applied is not able to resolve a claim,
negotiate a settlement of the matter, obtain necessary licenses
on commercially reasonable terms, and/or successfully prosecute
or defend its position, Applied&#146;s business, financial

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied is subject to various risks related to:
(1)&nbsp;new, different, inconsistent or even conflicting laws,
rules and regulations that may be enacted by legislative bodies
and/or regulatory agencies in the countries in which Applied
operates and with which Applied must comply; and
(2)&nbsp;disagreements or disputes between national or regional
regulatory agencies related to international trade.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For example, the World Trade Organization (WTO)
has determined that the United States Foreign Sales Corporation
(FSC) and Extraterritorial Income (ETI) exclusions constitute
prohibited export subsidies. Legislation currently pending in
the United States Congress may eliminate the FSC and ETI tax
provisions but may also contain other provisions that offset the
elimination of these tax benefits. Applied has benefited from
FSC and ETI tax provisions, and the elimination of these tax
provisions without any financially comparable replacement tax
benefits could materially and adversely affect Applied&#146;s
financial condition and results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During fiscal 2002, Applied filed an application
with the SEC for an exemptive order confirming that it is not
subject to the Investment Company Act of 1940 (the Act), which
requires companies primarily engaged in the business of
investing in securities to comply with additional rules and
regulations. Based on Applied&#146;s ratios of investments to
total assets and of interest income to net income, Applied could
be deemed to be covered by the Act. In March 2004, Applied
responded to the SEC&#146;s request for additional and updated
information. If the SEC does not grant the exemption, Applied
may have to take other actions that could adversely affect its
results of operations in order not to be subject to the Act.

    <B><I><FONT size="2">Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied purchases forward exchange and currency
option contracts to hedge certain existing and anticipated
foreign currency denominated transactions expected to occur
during the next year. Gains and losses on these contracts are
generally recognized in income when the related transactions
being hedged are recognized. Net foreign currency gains and
losses were not material for the three or six months ended
April&nbsp;27, 2003 and May&nbsp;2, 2004. Because the effect of
movements in currency exchange rates on forward exchange and
currency option contracts generally offsets the related effect
on the underlying items being hedged, these financial
instruments are not expected to subject Applied to risks that
would otherwise result from changes in currency exchange rates.
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">Applied has performed an analysis to assess the
potential financial effect of reasonably possible near-term
changes in interest and foreign currency exchange rates. Based
upon Applied&#146;s analysis, the effect of such rate changes is
not expected to be material to Applied&#146;s financial
condition, results of operations or cash flows.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As required by Rule&nbsp;13a-15(b) of the
Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, Applied management,
including its Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial
Officer, conducted an evaluation as of the end of the period
covered by this report, of the effectiveness of Applied&#146;s
disclosure controls and procedures as defined in
Rule&nbsp;13a-15(e). Based on that evaluation, the Chief
Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer concluded that
Applied&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures were effective
as of the end of the period covered by this report. As required
by Rule&nbsp;13a-15(d), Applied management, including its Chief
Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, also conducted an
evaluation of Applied&#146;s internal control over financial
reporting to determine whether any changes occurred during the
quarter that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely
to materially affect, Applied&#146;s internal control over
financial reporting. Based on that evaluation, there has been no
such change during the quarter.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">It should be noted that any system of controls,
however well designed and operated, can provide only reasonable,
and not absolute, assurance that the objectives of the system
will be met. In addition, the design of any control system is
based in part upon certain assumptions about the likelihood of
future events.
</FONT>

<!-- link1 "PART II. OTHER INFORMATION" -->

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">PART&nbsp;II.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OTHER
INFORMATION</FONT></B>

<DIV align="left">
<A name='107'></A>
</DIV>

<!-- link1 "Item 1. Legal Proceedings" -->

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="8%"></TD>
    <TD width="92%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><B><FONT size="2">Item&nbsp;1.</FONT></B></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Legal Proceedings</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Novellus</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On June&nbsp;13, 1997, after Varian Associates,
Inc. (Varian) failed to respond to requests by Applied to
discuss certain patent issues, Applied filed a lawsuit against
Varian captioned Applied Materials, Inc.&nbsp;v. Varian
Associates, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;C-97-20523-RMW) in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California,
alleging infringement of several of Applied&#146;s patents
concerning PVD technology. On July&nbsp;7, 1997, Applied amended
that action to allege infringement of those same Applied PVD
patents against Novellus Systems, Inc. (Novellus) and to add
Novellus as a defendant, as a result of Novellus&#146;
acquisition of Varian&#146;s thin film systems PVD business. On
June&nbsp;23, 1997, Novellus filed a separate lawsuit against
Applied captioned Novellus Systems, Inc.&nbsp;v. Applied
Materials, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;C-97-20551-EAI) in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California,
alleging infringement by Applied of several PVD technology
patents that were formerly owned by Varian. Novellus seeks
damages for past infringement, a permanent injunction, treble
damages for willful infringement, pre-judgment interest and
attorneys&#146; fees. In September 2000, Applied and Varian
settled their disputes and Applied released all claims with
respect to the Inova system as it was made and sold as of
May&nbsp;7, 1997. On October&nbsp;3, 2000, Applied&#146;s claims
against Varian and Varian&#146;s claims and counterclaims
against Applied were dismissed with prejudice. The litigation
with Novellus continues. Discovery has closed in the actions.
The previously set trial date of May&nbsp;24, 2004 has been
rescheduled and trial now is set to begin on September&nbsp;20,
2004. Applied believes the September trial will involve only
infringement and validity issues regarding Novellus&#146; patent
claims against Applied and Applied&#146;s declaratory judgment
claims against Novellus&#146; patents. Applied believes it has
meritorious claims and defenses and intends to pursue them
vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Linear Technology</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On March&nbsp;2, 2001, Linear Technology Corp.
(LTC) filed a third party complaint against Applied in the
United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas,
captioned Texas Instruments, Inc.&nbsp;v. Linear Technology
Corp.&nbsp;v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;2-01-CV4
(DF)). The complaint against Applied alleged that Applied is
obligated to indemnify LTC and defend LTC for certain claims in
the underlying patent infringement lawsuit brought by Texas
Instruments, Inc. (TI) against LTC. The complaint also alleged
claims for breach of contract, breach of warranty, and various
unfair business practices. In the complaint, LTC
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">22
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">alleged that, before LTC purchased certain
equipment from Applied, Applied failed to disclose to LTC that
TI previously had won a jury verdict against Hyundai Electronics
Industries Co., Ltd. (Hyundai) for patent infringement based on
Hyundai&#146;s use of certain semiconductor equipment including
some Applied tools. LTC&#146;s Texas lawsuit against Applied
sought indemnification and damages from Applied and an order
requiring Applied to defend LTC in the underlying lawsuit with
TI. On January&nbsp;15, 2002, the court granted TI&#146;s motion
to sever Applied and the other third party defendants from the
action and dismissed LTC&#146;s action against Applied and the
other third party defendants without prejudice. On
March&nbsp;12, 2002, LTC filed a complaint against Applied in
the Superior Court for the County of Santa&nbsp;Clara, captioned
Linear Technology Corp.&nbsp;v. Applied Materials, Inc.,
Novellus Systems, Inc. and Tokyo Electron Ltd., (case
no.&nbsp;CV806004) alleging claims for breach of contract, fraud
and deceit, negligent misrepresentation, suppression of fact,
unfair competition, breach of warranty, express contractual
indemnity, implied equitable indemnity and declaratory relief.
On November&nbsp;12, 2002, LTC filed an amended complaint in the
Santa&nbsp;Clara action asserting essentially the same claims as
in the original complaint but adding an additional assertion
that LTC and TI have settled their litigation. Applied&#146;s
motion to dismiss the amended complaint was granted in part. LTC
filed a Second Amended Complaint and Applied&#146;s motion to
dismiss the Second Amended Complaint was granted. LTC filed a
Third Amended Complaint and Applied&#146;s motion to dismiss the
Third Amended Complaint was granted. On February&nbsp;13, 2004,
LTC filed a Fourth Amended Complaint. Applied has moved to
dismiss the Fourth Amended Complaint. Applied believes that it
has meritorious defenses and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">David Scharf</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On July&nbsp;31, 2001, David Scharf, an
individual, filed a lawsuit against Applied in the United States
District Court for the Central District of California, captioned
David Scharf&nbsp;v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case no. 01-06580
AHM). The lawsuit alleges that Applied has infringed, has
induced others to infringe and has contributed to others&#146;
infringement of a patent concerning color synthesizing scanning
electron microscope technology. Mr.&nbsp;Scharf seeks a
preliminary and permanent injunction, damages and costs. Applied
has answered the complaint and counterclaimed for declaratory
judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. On May&nbsp;10,
2002, Mr.&nbsp;Scharf filed a request for re-examination of his
patent with the Patent and Trademark Office. On June&nbsp;26,
2002, the case was removed from the Court&#146;s active docket
after the parties stipulated to stay the case pending the
results of that re-examination. On July&nbsp;11, 2002, Applied
filed its own request for re-examination of
Mr.&nbsp;Scharf&#146;s patent with the Patent and Trademark
Office. Applied&#146;s request for re-examination was granted on
September&nbsp;19, 2002. Applied believes it has meritorious
defenses and counterclaims and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">ASMI</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On August&nbsp;27, 2002, ASM America, Inc. and
ASM International, N.V. (collectively ASMI) filed a lawsuit
against Applied in the United States District Court for the
District of Arizona, captioned ASM America, Inc. and ASM
International, N.V.&nbsp;v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case
no.&nbsp;Civ&#146;02 1660 PHX SMM). The lawsuit sought a
judicial declaration that ASMI does not infringe six patents
belonging to Applied that relate to remote cleaning of CVD
chambers and to deposition of silicon nitride. The suit also
sought a judicial declaration that two of the six patents are
invalid. Applied moved for a more definitive statement with
respect to two of ASMI&#146;s causes of action. On
September&nbsp;29, 2003, the court granted Applied&#146;s motion
for a more definitive statement. ASMI filed an amended complaint
on October&nbsp;31, 2003. The amended lawsuit seeks a judicial
declaration that ASMI does not infringe the six patents and that
the six patents are invalid. On December&nbsp;15, 2003, Applied
answered the amended complaint by denying the allegations and
counterclaiming for infringement of the six patents. Applied
seeks damages, a preliminary and permanent injunction, costs and
attorneys&#146; fees. No trial date has been set. Applied
believes it has meritorious defenses and counterclaims and
intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On October&nbsp;3, 2003, ASMI filed a lawsuit
against Applied in the United States District Court for the
Eastern District of Texas, captioned ASM America, Inc. and ASM
International, N.V.&nbsp;v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case
no.&nbsp;2&nbsp;03CV 348 TJW). The lawsuit alleges infringement
of six ASMI patents and seeks damages
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">23
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">for past infringement, enhanced damages,
attorneys&#146; fees, and injunctive relief. Applied responded
to the complaint by denying the allegations and counterclaiming
for a declaratory judgment of invalidity, unenforceability and
non-infringement of the patents. Applied also has asserted that
ASMI is infringing seven Applied patents, including the six
patents at issue in the Arizona action plus an additional
patent. Applied seeks injunctive relief, compensatory and
enhanced damages, costs and attorneys&#146; fees. Applied has
filed a motion to transfer the case from the Eastern District of
Texas to the District of Arizona. The Court has set a trial date
of May&nbsp;2, 2005. Applied believes it has meritorious
defenses and counterclaims and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Varian Semiconductor Equipment Associates,
Inc.</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On September&nbsp;13, 2002, Varian Semiconductor
Equipment Associates, Inc. (VSEA) filed a demand for arbitration
with the American Arbitration Association asserting that Applied
has breached a patent license agreement between VSEA and Applied
dated January&nbsp;1, 1992. VSEA seeks to recover royalties,
interest and attorneys&#146; fees. The arbitration hearing on
whether the products are covered by the license agreement has
concluded. On May&nbsp;2, 2003, the arbitration panel issued an
interim decision finding that some, but not all, of the products
at issue were subject to the agreement. The arbitration panel
next will consider whether the asserted claims of the patents
under which those products were found to be covered are valid.
The arbitration hearing on those issues is scheduled to begin on
June&nbsp;26, 2004. Applied believes that it has meritorious
defenses and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Jusung</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On December&nbsp;24, 2003 (local Taiwan time),
Applied Materials, Inc. filed a lawsuit against Jusung
Engineering Co., Ltd., and Jusung Pacific Co., Ltd.,
(collectively Jusung) in Tao-Yuan District Court in Taiwan
captioned Applied Materials, Inc.&nbsp;v. Jusung Engineering
Co., Ltd. (case no.&nbsp;92 Tsai-chuan Tzi No.&nbsp;6388). The
lawsuit alleges that Jusung is infringing a patent related to
chemical vapor deposition owned by Applied. In the suit, Applied
seeks a provisional injunction prohibiting Jusung from
importing, using, manufacturing, servicing or selling in Taiwan
certain flat panel display manufacturing equipment. On
December&nbsp;25, 2003, the Tao-Yuan District Court ruled in
favor of Applied&#146;s request for a provisional injunction and
on January&nbsp;14, 2004, the Court issued a provisional
injunction order. Jusung has appealed those decisions. On
January&nbsp;30, 2004, Jusung sought permission to post a
counterbond to have the injunction lifted. Jusung&#146;s
application was granted and, on March&nbsp;30, 2004, the
provisional injunction order was lifted. Applied appealed the
counterbond decisions and, on May&nbsp;31, 2004, the appellate
court ruled that the injunction should be reinstated pending a
final decision on Applied&#146;s appeal of the grant of the
counterbond. Applied believes it has meritorious claims and
intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Taiwan Fair Trade Commission</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;10, 2004, the Taiwan Fair Trade
Commission (TFTC) notified Applied&#146;s subsidiary AKT, Inc.
(AKT) in Taiwan that, pursuant to a complaint filed by Jusung,
the TFTC had begun an investigation into whether AKT violated
the Taiwan Fair Trade Act. The investigation focuses on whether
AKT violated the Taiwan Guidelines for the Review of Cases
Involving Enterprises Issuing Warning Letters for Infringement
on Copyright, Trademark and Patent Rights by allegedly notifying
customers about AKT&#146;s patent rights and the infringement of
those rights by Jusung. Although Applied believes there has been
no violation, neither the extent nor the outcome of the
investigation can be determined at this time. Applied believes
that the outcome will not have a material adverse effect on its
financial condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Other Legal Matters</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">From time to time, Applied receives notification
from customers claiming that such customers are entitled to
indemnification or other obligations from Applied related to
infringement claims made against the customers by third parties.
In addition, Applied is subject to various other legal
proceedings and claims, either asserted or unasserted, that
arise in the ordinary course of business. Although the outcome
of these claims
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">24
</FONT>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">cannot be predicted with certainty, Applied does
not believe that any of these other existing legal proceedings
will have a material adverse effect on its financial condition
or results of operations.
</FONT>
</DIV>

                                                                    EXHIBIT 31.1

                                  CERTIFICATION

I, Michael R. Splinter, certify that:

         1.       I have reviewed this quarterly report on Form 10-Q of Applied
                  Materials, Inc.;

         2.       Based on my knowledge, this report does not contain any untrue
                  statement of a material fact or omit to state a material fact
                  necessary to make the statements made, in light of the
                  circumstances under which such statements were made, not
                  misleading with respect to the period covered by this report;

         3.       Based on my knowledge, the financial statements, and other
                  financial information included in this report, fairly present
                  in all material respects the financial condition, results of
                  operations and cash flows of the registrant as of, and for,
                  the periods presented in this report;

         4.       The registrant's other certifying officer and I are
                  responsible for establishing and maintaining disclosure
                  controls and procedures (as defined in Exchange Act Rules
                  13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e)) for the registrant and have:

                  (a)      Designed such disclosure controls and procedures, or
                           caused such disclosure controls and procedures to be
                           designed under our supervision, to ensure that
                           material information relating to the registrant,
                           including its consolidated subsidiaries, is made
                           known to us by others within those entities,
                           particularly during the period in which this report
                           is being prepared;

                  (b)      Evaluated the effectiveness of the registrant's
                           disclosure controls and procedures and presented in
                           this report our conclusions about the effectiveness
                           of the disclosure controls and procedures, as of the
                           end of the period covered by this report based on
                           such evaluation; and

                  (c)      Disclosed in this report any change in the
                           registrant's internal control over financial
                           reporting that occurred during the registrant's most
                           recent fiscal quarter (the registrant's fourth fiscal
                           quarter in the case of an annual report) that has
                           materially affected, or is reasonably likely to
                           materially affect, the registrant's internal control
                           over financial reporting; and

         5.       The registrant's other certifying officer and I have
                  disclosed, based on our most recent evaluation of internal
                  control over financial reporting, to the registrant's auditors
                  and the audit committee of the registrant's board of directors
                  (or persons performing the equivalent functions):

                  (a)      All significant deficiencies and material weaknesses
                           in the design or operation of internal control over
                           financial reporting which are reasonably likely to
                           adversely affect the registrant's ability to record,
                           process, summarize and report financial information;
                           and

                  (b)      Any fraud, whether or not material, that involves
                           management or other employees who have a significant
                           role in the registrant's internal control over
                           financial reporting.

Date: June 10, 2004

                                               By:  /s/ MICHAEL R. SPLINTER
                                                    ----------------------------
                                                    Michael R. Splinter
                                                    President and Chief
                                                    Executive Officer

</TEXT>
</DOCUMENT>

                                                                    EXHIBIT 32.1

                             APPLIED MATERIALS, INC.

                  SARBANES-OXLEY ACT SECTION 906 CERTIFICATION

In connection with this quarterly report on Form 10-Q of Applied Materials, Inc.
for the period ended May 2, 2004, I, Michael R. Splinter, President and Chief
Executive Officer of Applied Materials, Inc., hereby certify pursuant to 18
U.S.C.Section 1350, as adopted pursuant to Section 906 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act
of 2002, that:

         1.       this Form 10-Q for the period ended May 2, 2004 fully complies
                  with the requirements of section 13(a) or 15(d) of the
                  Securities Exchange Act of 1934; and

         2.       the information contained in this Form 10-Q for the period
                  ended May 2, 2004 fairly presents, in all material respects,
                  the financial condition and results of operations of Applied
                  Materials, Inc. for the periods presented therein.

Date: June 10, 2004

                                                   By:   /s/ MICHAEL R. SPLINTER
                                                         -----------------------
                                                         Michael R. Splinter
                                                         President and Chief
                                                         Executive Officer

                                                                    Exhibit 99.1


EARNINGS TO FIXED CHARGES

The ratio of earnings to fixed charges for the six months ended April 27, 2003
and May 2, 2004, and for each of the last five fiscal years, was as follows:

<TABLE>
<CAPTION>
                                                                                     Six Months Ended
                                                                                   --------------------
                                   Fiscal Year                                     April 27,     May 2,
- --------------------------------------------------------------------------
      1999             2000           2001          2002            2003            2003         2004
      ----             ----           ----          ----            ----            ----        -----
<S>                   <C>            <C>            <C>             <C>             <C>        <C>
     14.03x           32.82x         11.80x         4.58x            (a)             (b)       17.71x
     ======           ======         ======         =====            ===             ===       ======
</TABLE>


(a)  Due to Applied's loss in fiscal 2003, the ratio of coverage was less than
     1:1. Applied would have needed to generate additional earnings of $209
     million to achieve the coverage ratio of 1:1.

(b)  Due to Applied's loss for the six months ended April 27, 2003, the ratio of
     coverage was less than 1:1. Applied would have needed to generate
     additional earnings of $180 million to achieve the coverage ratio of 1:1.
